Now, enter the world of <em>Neanderthal</em>...<br /><br />The expedition of the century...uncovers the find of the millennium...<em>Neanderthal</em>.<br /><br />In the remote mountains of central Asia, an eminent Harvard archeologist discovers something extraordinary. He sends a cryptic message to two colleagues. But then, he disappears.<br /><br />Matt Ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8547359385238592834">Not since <em>Jurassic Park</em> has a novel so enthralled readers everywhere. Now, enter the world of <em>Neanderthal</em>...<br /><br />The expedition of the century...uncovers the find of the millennium...<em>Neanderthal</em>.<br /><br />In the remote mountains of central Asia, an eminent Harvard archeologist discovers something extraordinary. He sends a cryptic message to two colleagues. But then, he disappears.<br /><br />Matt Mattison and Susan Arnot-- once lovers, now academic rivals-- are going where few humans have ever walked, looking for a relic band of creatures that have existed for over 40,000 years, that possess powers man can only imagine, and that are about to change the face of civilization forever.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_121212159">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121212159" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/687820-orin" class="left imgcol" title="Orin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1252526114p2/687820.jpg" alt="Orin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/121212159?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 11, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/687820-orin" class="user" title="Orin">Orin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer121212159">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8629437402118035936">Plot holes, flat characters, cliched twists, poor research, logical flaws, and a horrifyingly unsatisfactory ending that uses Bruce Springsteen to terrorize primitive man. What's not to like?<br /><br />This is the kind of book that lovers of prehistoric fiction, or lovers of techno-thriller (read: Crichton and imitators) should love. Being both, I must report painfully otherwise. Why? Just plain sloppiness. Understand that I don't have a problem with dumb: give me a simple plot and a juicy payoff and I can</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8629437402118035936">Plot holes, flat characters, cliched twists, poor research, logical flaws, and a horrifyingly unsatisfactory ending that uses Bruce Springsteen to terrorize primitive man. What's not to like?<br /><br />This is the kind of book that lovers of prehistoric fiction, or lovers of techno-thriller (read: Crichton and imitators) should love. Being both, I must report painfully otherwise. Why? Just plain sloppiness. Understand that I don't have a problem with dumb: give me a simple plot and a juicy payoff and I can be happy. However, if the author insists on poking me in the eye by writing inconsistent descriptions, destroying objects then bringing them back pages later unexplained, switching between different points of view unannounced, forgetting his own character's motivations, developing threads only to discard them needlessly, and refusing to use an editor for more than spellcheck, well, I WILL THROW YOUR BOOK IN THE GARBAGE. <br /><br />I am beset by a few lingering questions: how do you watch an avalanche from the mouth of a cave under it? Are non-extinct cave bears just a bonus any time you discover stone age people? Why is there so much firewood above the treeline? Do you know the difference between paleontologist and archeologist? Did you read the books and articles in your bibliography? Have you ever been camping? Have you ever met a scientist, a Russian, or a military officer? Have you ever met a woman who likes the phrase "pubic mound?" Do you hate your readers? Do you hate Bruce Springsteen? Have I proved my point yet?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8629437402118035936">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_261087041">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261087041" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1410180-kimberly" class="left imgcol" title="Kimberly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1414363793p2/1410180.jpg" alt="Kimberly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/261087041?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1410180-kimberly" class="user" title="Kimberly">Kimberly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/742770.Neanderthal" title="Hardcover 9780679449782" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1410180-kimberly?shelf=2012-bookshelf" class="actionLinkLite">2012-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1410180-kimberly?shelf=library-books-read-2012" class="actionLinkLite">library-books-read-2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1410180-kimberly?shelf=monsters-dinos-prehistoric-beasts" class="actionLinkLite">monsters-dinos-prehistoric-beasts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer261087041">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17497942887564106888"><strong> 4.5 Stars</strong><br /><br />Many of you know that I am an avid history buff with an affinity for the prehistoric so when I accidentally stumbled upon a link to this book I was so excited to read it I put it on hold at the library right away. <br /><br />I thought the story was unique and pretty damn near perfect. It's about Matt, Susan and their mentor Kellicut who discover two lost tribes of neanderthals living in a remote part of Asia. <br /><br />What I really liked about the book was all the adventure that was packed into the 368 pa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17497942887564106888"><strong> 4.5 Stars</strong><br /><br />Many of you know that I am an avid history buff with an affinity for the prehistoric so when I accidentally stumbled upon a link to this book I was so excited to read it I put it on hold at the library right away. <br /><br />I thought the story was unique and pretty damn near perfect. It's about Matt, Susan and their mentor Kellicut who discover two lost tribes of neanderthals living in a remote part of Asia. <br /><br />What I really liked about the book was all the adventure that was packed into the 368 pages. While I was reading other peoples reviews about the book on Goodreads one of the things I noticed was that people were saying it was far fetched. IT'S FICTION PEOPLE. If people can right books where there are bat like alien species and not get told that it's unrealistic how can you judge this piece of FICTION and say it is unrealistic? Is it because it upsets your delicate sensibilities? Should the fictional writing of a lost prehistoric tribe really incite such anger and disbelief when people unquestioningly read books where vampires, werewolves and a whole other assortment of creatures run rampant? I believe that that's something worth mulling over. I for one LOVED that this book was published because I have a genuine interest in the prehistoric era. <br /><br />I thought the writing in this was pretty good. Yes there were a few places where it seemed to jump around sporadically but that is not uncommon in a book. It happens whether we like it or hate it it will happen. There were also some places where I found the author repeating phrases a little too much but that too is nothing to fret over. However, I do wish that there was a wee bit more to the back stories of Matt and Susan and their relationship but I get the fact that it is not a romance novel but the romantic in me still wishes there was still something more. <br /><br />I found the whole premise to be intriguing. I mean telepathic neanderthals living in a remote part of Asia...what more could I ask for?! This book mixed history and science fiction together in such a way that it left me wishing that this were a true story. I can't tell you how many times I've dreamt of making such a discovery. Silly I know but sometimes the dreams we had as children are still the best dreams of all. This book let one of my dreams come to life and let me feel like I was in the story with Matt and Susan fighting to survive and rescue each other when captured by the opposing tribe of neanderthals who just happen to like to eat the brains of their enemies. Yum! <br /><br />All in all it was in my opinion a near perfect book for me and I recommend it to everyone! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17497942887564106888">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/63599-rob" class="user" title="Rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/63599-rob?shelf=speculative-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">speculative-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer41402612'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41402612">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3066202814630866537">I read this back at the end of high school. I was drawn to it by the skull on the cover, and because Discover magazine, which I was obsessed with at the time, had run article after article on human evolution.<br /><br />The book is based on the premise that Neanderthals still exist, and an enclave is discovered. Moreover, the reason that humans defeated them is that they are peace-loving animals, and they are peace loving because they have telepathic powers that basically create a sense of empathy that make</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3066202814630866537">I read this back at the end of high school. I was drawn to it by the skull on the cover, and because Discover magazine, which I was obsessed with at the time, had run article after article on human evolution.<br /><br />The book is based on the premise that Neanderthals still exist, and an enclave is discovered. Moreover, the reason that humans defeated them is that they are peace-loving animals, and they are peace loving because they have telepathic powers that basically create a sense of empathy that makes it hard for them to be violent.<br /><br />There's also a love story in there in which the main character and his ex-wife get back together, and a weird sex scene in which, while Neanderthals are pairing off to make the Whoopie, they can't help themselves and do the same.<br /><br />Weird book. Not very good. At the point in my life that I read it I steadfastly refused not to finish any book I started, so I did finish it, but it's safe to say that I'll never read it again.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/139508684?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4709664-c-d-leavitt" class="user" title="C.D. Leavitt">C.D. Leavitt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4709664-c-d-leavitt?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer139508684">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7265840262017280430">This is quite possibly one of the worst books I've ever read. It was so bad that just looking at the cover now made me laugh as I remembered how truly dreadful it was.<br /><br />Fantastic elements like a hidden, lost world in Asia where psychic Neanderthals continue to live in isolation are one thing. The atrocious writing, utter disregard of even the most cursory of research on what sort of technology Neanderthals had, and the pulpy obsession with sex made it seem like a book from another time. The fact t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7265840262017280430">This is quite possibly one of the worst books I've ever read. It was so bad that just looking at the cover now made me laugh as I remembered how truly dreadful it was.<br /><br />Fantastic elements like a hidden, lost world in Asia where psychic Neanderthals continue to live in isolation are one thing. The atrocious writing, utter disregard of even the most cursory of research on what sort of technology Neanderthals had, and the pulpy obsession with sex made it seem like a book from another time. The fact that it came out in the mid '90s rather than a few decades earlier astounds me.<br /><br />As other reviewers have mentioned, this was full of plot holes and the characters have about as much depth as the paper they're written on. The Neanderthals are written more like shrieking, hopping ape-men than close relatives to humans and they come in only two flavors: murderous monkeys or hippies.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7265840262017280430">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_637074368">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637074368" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4338068-christina" class="left imgcol" title="Christina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1285470493p2/4338068.jpg" alt="Christina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/637074368?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 19, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4338068-christina" class="user" title="Christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/742770.Neanderthal" title="Hardcover 9780679449782" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4338068-christina?shelf=stinker-of-the-year" class="actionLinkLite">stinker-of-the-year</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4338068-christina?shelf=finished-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">finished-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer637074368">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7581644134820131164">Book #31 for 2013<br /><br />Want to read something that makes <strong>Deception Point</strong> look like great literature? This is it. It's like the author vaguely remembered something from the Anthropology 101 he took 20-some-odd years ago, thought it might make a neat premise for a story, and then, without doing any further research, whipped out this peurile tale of horny archaeologists and modern-day cavemen. Seriously, I've seen better plotting, character development, and attention to detail in Geico commercials.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_396370185">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396370185" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt" class="left imgcol" title="Matt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444448460p2/5903843.jpg" alt="Matt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/396370185?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 27, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt" class="user" title="Matt">Matt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer396370185">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1196139706652548733">Darnton uses his first novel to open up a long disputed issue; the decline of the Neanderthal. While I read the book, I became convinced that Darnton is an archeologist, wanting to implant his own ideas to the reader in a fiction-based setting. I was shocked to see that his CV includes a great deal of media experience, but nothing scholastic related to the subject. Darnton not only takes the reader to the centre of the debate, but also posits numerous theories and backs them up in such a way tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1196139706652548733">Darnton uses his first novel to open up a long disputed issue; the decline of the Neanderthal. While I read the book, I became convinced that Darnton is an archeologist, wanting to implant his own ideas to the reader in a fiction-based setting. I was shocked to see that his CV includes a great deal of media experience, but nothing scholastic related to the subject. Darnton not only takes the reader to the centre of the debate, but also posits numerous theories and backs them up in such a way that it keeps the reader interested. He also keeps the story as realistic as possible and away from anything too sci-fi and out there. Where he does venture into realism/sci fi territory, he does so in an attempt to teach or have the reader learn and posit their own conclusions.<br /><br />In a short period of time, Darnton examines the decline of the Neanderthals and what may have cuased their demise. He also layers on a story about science wanting to study and examine them, as well as a somewhat cheesy romance to keep the story rolling. While some of it was, perhaps, unneeded, the story does flow well and keeps the reader interested, at least enough to want to know what is going to happen. With numerous teaching moments and a great deal of history intertwined into the story, Darnton keeps the info flowing and tackles some of the larger issues.<br /><br />Kudos Mr. Darnton. I look forward to your other works, which seem just as scientifically based.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1196139706652548733">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_168051420">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168051420" itemprop="url" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/168051420?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 31, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5152397-tamara-rose-blodgett" class="user" title="Tamara Rose Blodgett">Tamara Rose Blodgett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5152397-tamara-rose-blodgett?shelf=drama" class="actionLinkLite">drama</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5152397-tamara-rose-blodgett?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5152397-tamara-rose-blodgett?shelf=paranormal-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer168051420">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5400773587624272922">People from all different walks of life are disappearing in the wildly remote, Pamir Mountains. When a shady American government agency hears local lore that strange, humanoid creatures have been taking people for hundreds of years, they launch an endeavor shrouded in deceit and exploitation.<br /><br />Commandeering [Harvard] Professor Kellicut ( for the government's nefarious purposes) and given superficial revelations only, Kellicut begins an expedition which he soon discovers that keeping any findings s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5400773587624272922">People from all different walks of life are disappearing in the wildly remote, Pamir Mountains. When a shady American government agency hears local lore that strange, humanoid creatures have been taking people for hundreds of years, they launch an endeavor shrouded in deceit and exploitation.<br /><br />Commandeering [Harvard] Professor Kellicut ( for the government's nefarious purposes) and given superficial revelations only, Kellicut begins an expedition which he soon discovers that keeping any findings silent may save his life. When the agency loses contact with Kellicut, they enlist ( under false pretenses) two former lovers and current scientist rivals to locate Kellicut. <br /><br />They soon embrace the search when clues lead to a reality Scientists Mattison and Arnot could have never postulated. What they begin to discover throws all theories their colleagues had ascribed out the window. When a species of (supposedly) extinct humanoids are discovered, excitement turns to horror as differences endanger the expedition and it's revealed the “creatures” have an extraordinary means of communication that is both wondrous and devastating to Mattison and Arnot's very survival.<br /><br />An absolute great read that is fast-paced, interesting and thrilling, it will appeal to evolutionary theorists, fantasy, wilderness and mystery lovers. I read this in one day, it was a couldn't-put-it-down book. Darnton is a very strong writer who won a Pulitzer Prize for stories he smuggled out of Poland during martial law. The strength of this novel is it's natural prose, where one never “sees” the mechanics of Darnton writing; flawless!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3237984956181250562">Neanderthals are out there? Still alive? Hell, I could have told you that! I’ve worked with a few. They are all in middle management! And I think someone actually made a TV movie out of this book. It must have been as bad. The idea is good and the book starts out like any typical anthropological thriller.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText3237984956181250562">Neanderthals are out there? Still alive? Hell, I could have told you that! I’ve worked with a few. They are all in middle management! And I think someone actually made a TV movie out of this book. It must have been as bad. The idea is good and the book starts out like any typical anthropological thriller. The characters are made from discarded plastic and once past the mumble-science the story has no where to go except to start killing off either the subjects or protagonists (not a bad idea for either). Some of the worst dialogue ever. I was so in the mood for another “Jurassic Park.” Instead I got “Utopia.” I made it to the end because I wanted to get my flea market $1’s worth.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1182039116">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1182039116" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9925031-sasha" class="left imgcol" title="Sasha"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1338538823p2/9925031.jpg" alt="Sasha" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1182039116?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9925031-sasha" class="user" title="Sasha">Sasha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1182039116">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1886715275360807862">It was entertaining and it held my attention, but at the end it turned out just as I expected, fluffy read. <br />I guess this could probably be used as a basis for a adventure movie, because its very cinematic - two professors (lovers long ago, how conveniently) are sent in a deserted wilderness to found out whereabouts of third professor who had disappeared while searching for signs of Bigfoot, Yeti or possibly surviving Neanderthals. What is maddening is that this fluffy little bite could have been</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1886715275360807862">It was entertaining and it held my attention, but at the end it turned out just as I expected, fluffy read. <br />I guess this could probably be used as a basis for a adventure movie, because its very cinematic - two professors (lovers long ago, how conveniently) are sent in a deserted wilderness to found out whereabouts of third professor who had disappeared while searching for signs of Bigfoot, Yeti or possibly surviving Neanderthals. What is maddening is that this fluffy little bite could have been so much more if only author was just a little bit more ambitious - he clearly knows his way around the subject, because he mentions enough names to assure you he is fascinated with it. For whatever reasons, it all ends up boxed into typical thriller-adventure cliché (with unavoidable explosion &amp; fire at the end) which really makes the whole story pointless and very lightweight. Somewhere deep inside there is a interesting message and a little bit of sadness - at least this is how personally I feel it - about our long lost relative. And surely, if we happen to find a surviving one, we would probably poke, pinch and stuck needles in him before we turn him into circus attraction. Not long ago I have visited a Neanderthal museum in Krapina, Croatia so this is all a very real, serious issue with me. I refuse to think they were in any way inferior to us.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1886715275360807862">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_947772596">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947772596" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16890356-dan-parrott" class="left imgcol" title="Dan Parrott"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1359381053p2/16890356.jpg" alt="Dan Parrott" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/947772596?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16890356-dan-parrott" class="user" title="Dan Parrott">Dan Parrott</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer947772596">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5993317862663336845">I ended this book conflicted. On the one hand, I think the "science" part of the book overtook the "fiction" part early on. This made for a story driven by the science, as opposed to a good story. Maybe it's because it just didn't rise to the level of some of the other stand-outs in this genre (think Descent by Jeff Long, anything by Douglas Preston and Lincoln Child, or Tom Knox's novels), but again those are some pretty heady company. The science didn't get crazy, and the action didn't get stu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5993317862663336845">I ended this book conflicted. On the one hand, I think the "science" part of the book overtook the "fiction" part early on. This made for a story driven by the science, as opposed to a good story. Maybe it's because it just didn't rise to the level of some of the other stand-outs in this genre (think Descent by Jeff Long, anything by Douglas Preston and Lincoln Child, or Tom Knox's novels), but again those are some pretty heady company. The science didn't get crazy, and the action didn't get stupid (sorry James Rollins, looking at you), but it just didn't overcome the story issues. On the other hand, the author DID get the ending right. If you've read much modern fiction, I think you might agree with the fact that the ending is just hard to nail sometimes. Even my favorite authors sometimes stumble across the finish line, despite an amazing race for the first 456 pages. So kudos for a good ending, but it just wasn't strong enough storywise to rate higher. Too intelligent for a beach read, yet not a good enough tale for a serious read. If you're bored and only if you want to feel conflicted during and after you finish the book, go for it. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5993317862663336845">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_935947008">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/935947008" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6016465-lauri" class="left imgcol" title="Lauri"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1400696488p2/6016465.jpg" alt="Lauri" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/935947008?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 13, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6016465-lauri" class="user" title="Lauri">Lauri</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer935947008">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14251010335767419549">This was a thriller in the vein of James Rollins, although not quite as well-written (and I totally missed those author notes at the end of the book that Rollins always does, in which he separates fact from fiction for the readers). The premise was really cool: much of the remote regions of the world remain relatively unexplored, and we are continually discovering new species. Would it then be possible that, high in the mountains of Tajikstan (or elsewhere), small bands of Neanderthals could hav</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14251010335767419549">This was a thriller in the vein of James Rollins, although not quite as well-written (and I totally missed those author notes at the end of the book that Rollins always does, in which he separates fact from fiction for the readers). The premise was really cool: much of the remote regions of the world remain relatively unexplored, and we are continually discovering new species. Would it then be possible that, high in the mountains of Tajikstan (or elsewhere), small bands of Neanderthals could have survived (and in fact thrived)? I also found intriguing the exploration of language and its role in evolution; although many scientists assume that developing language may be the reason for the rise of Homo Sapiens, what if that language development took the place of a non-verbal form of communication (such as a form of ESP)? Another interesting debate, of course, is the one about what actually makes a society civilized; if we are warmongers, are we really more civilized than those who are more peaceful and equanimous? Finally, there was also the moral question that many anthropologists face: how to be an impartial observer without impacting the society or culture which one is observing. I enjoyed this book, and the story kept me on the edge of my seat. Even more, I like the idea of entertaining these questions...and I think they deserve discussion. This would be a great book club selection for that reason! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14251010335767419549">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I'm looking forward to reading the other two. <br /><br />Neanderthals have developed a radically different civilization on a parallel Earth. A Neanderthal physicist, Ponter Boddit, accidentally passes from his universe into a Canadian underground research facility. Fortunately, a team of human scientists, including expert paleo-anthropologist Mary Vaughan, promptly identifies and warmly receives Ponter. Solving the language problem and much else is a mini-computer, called a Companion, implanted in the brain of every Neanderthal. A computerized guardian spirit, however, doesn't eliminate cross-cultural confusion; permanent male-female sexuality, rape, and overpopulation are all alien to Ponter. Nor can it help his housemate and fellow scientist back in his world, Adikor Huld, when the authorities charge Adikor with his murder. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18076507098997983333">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11008006727581437036">This waiting room lightweight had some potential--at least as far as the topic was concerned--but as it progressed, it quickly became apparent that the author couldn't decide to go for Michael Crichton's <em>Jurassic Park</em> or Gary Jennings' <em>Aztec</em> as his creative inspiration, so he split it down the middle. A team of paleoanthropologists pursue a yeti sighting as potential Neanderthal progenitors and find a Shangri-La near the Himalayas with “Nobel Savage” occupants that possess ESP as their means of communication. These “pure” souls are then found to be locked into a symbiotic relationship with an “evil” tribe of the same species...need I say more? Wait! Does this sound like the Eloi and the Morlocks? Okay, maybe Jules Vern's <em>The Time Machine</em> was the actual inspiration.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_674837866">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674837866" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1973256-sue" class="left imgcol" title="Sue"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1284656041p2/1973256.jpg" alt="Sue" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/674837866?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 23, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1973256-sue" class="user" title="Sue">Sue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer674837866">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13935870881572583987">Darnton's best-selling adventure about scientists who discover a lost race of Neanderthals in Afghanistan is an obvious choice for libraries, so let us only observe that Jay O. Saunders does a good job of narration and move on to other thoughts. The back of the box reads, "Far away, in the mountains of Northern Asia, a guerrilla fighter vanishes, a schoolgirl is murdered, and an eminent Harvard paleontologist disappears." The listener hears about only the last of these three items, but it doesn'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13935870881572583987">Darnton's best-selling adventure about scientists who discover a lost race of Neanderthals in Afghanistan is an obvious choice for libraries, so let us only observe that Jay O. Saunders does a good job of narration and move on to other thoughts. The back of the box reads, "Far away, in the mountains of Northern Asia, a guerrilla fighter vanishes, a schoolgirl is murdered, and an eminent Harvard paleontologist disappears." The listener hears about only the last of these three items, but it doesn't matter. Modern escape fiction, too jerky and dialog-heavy for unabridged recordings, lends itself to abridgment perfectly well without losing much stylistic integrity. Yes, one notices characters whizzing by without much development, but one suspects that there isn't all that much more in the full novel. Finally, although it would seem impossible to review this book without mentioning a certain other best-selling writer, we should do Darnton the favor of realizing that he falls squarely into the "lost race" tradition of H. Rider Haggard, Arthur Conan Doyle, and others from the turn of the century (though without the racism). A safe choice for all popular collections.?Michael Barrett, San Antonio P.L., Tex.<br />Copyright 1996</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13935870881572583987">...more</a>

          </span>

                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer40575079">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12041644909111347022">This was a jolly good adventure story! The plot was incredible, to say the least: the hero and heroine Matt &amp; Susan, long-parted lovers, are lured by the CIA to the Pamirs (mountains in one of those roof-of-the-world Russian republics) to seek out a colleague who disappeared on a hunt for Neanderthals. There's a series of heart-stopping encounters with the tribe that turns out to be the most advanced because they've learned to kill, but Matt &amp; Simon escape to live with a highly idealised</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12041644909111347022">This was a jolly good adventure story! The plot was incredible, to say the least: the hero and heroine Matt &amp; Susan, long-parted lovers, are lured by the CIA to the Pamirs (mountains in one of those roof-of-the-world Russian republics) to seek out a colleague who disappeared on a hunt for Neanderthals. There's a series of heart-stopping encounters with the tribe that turns out to be the most advanced because they've learned to kill, but Matt &amp; Simon escape to live with a highly idealised Eden with a more pacific group who mourn over the death of a fish caught by Matt. <br />It all seems credible enough for most of the story with authentic-sounding references to Darwin and other scientists we've vaguely heard of, but credulity is stretched to the limit by the final rescue of Susan. Earlier rescues involved improbably training some of the hominids to fight so that the evil Van (a CIA stooge accompanying the expedition) can be rescued; they take the risk because religion has taught them the sanctity of life. (Too bad so many of the hominids die because he's a worthless rat). But when the hominids make a Trojan horse to rescue Susan, (because deception is the key characteristic of homo sapiens, which enabled them to triumph over the Neanderthals) - well, that's when I started skipping paragraphs because it was so silly.<br />Still, it would make a great movie, with beaut battle scenes, apocalyptic earthquakes and exciting flights from terror. But they'd have a bit of trouble getting it released for general viewing if they included the torture of KeeWah's victims and the haunting image of the captured Neanderthal experimented on by the CIA (hoping to get an edge on the Russians by finding the secret of their telepathic communication).<br />Well, I did say it was silly...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12041644909111347022">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_579731146">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579731146" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5801980-jeff" class="left imgcol" title="Jeff"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1315257771p2/5801980.jpg" alt="Jeff" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/579731146?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5801980-jeff" class="user" title="Jeff">Jeff</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/742770.Neanderthal" title="Hardcover 9780679449782" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer579731146">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16749109819392611965">I bought this book in 1996. It was an impulse buy. I was really into novels with a science component. Mostly this consisted of Michael Crichton novels. I spotted this book on the new release shelf and thought it might be good. I took it home and put it on the shelf but never got around to reading it. It came with me through half a dozen moves waiting to be read. I finally decided to read it so I could get rid of it. Not that I knew if it was good or bad but somewhere along the way I just lost in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16749109819392611965">I bought this book in 1996. It was an impulse buy. I was really into novels with a science component. Mostly this consisted of Michael Crichton novels. I spotted this book on the new release shelf and thought it might be good. I took it home and put it on the shelf but never got around to reading it. It came with me through half a dozen moves waiting to be read. I finally decided to read it so I could get rid of it. Not that I knew if it was good or bad but somewhere along the way I just lost interest. Apparently I was more prescient than I would have guessed. The book isn't very good.<br /><br />The basic premise is that neanderthals survived through the ages in a few small communities in the mountains of central Asia. Eventually a shady government group figures out where they are and sends an expedition to seek them out and discover their "secrets".<br /><br />That's about all the synopsis you need because you aren't actually going to read this book. The science in this is laughable and the actions of the professional scientists are a complete joke. I realize that modern science doesn't have the Prime Directive but I think there is at least an understanding of what it means not to interfere with a population. The scientists in this book are leaders in their fields but have no problem completely disrupting the neanderthal way of life. Not only that but they jump right in to an extreme weather expedition with absolutely no training or experience. The entire novel is completely unbelievable and poorly written.<br /><br />I am glad I have finally read the book but I won't be sad to see it leave my library.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16749109819392611965">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18239170479386313075">When I first saw this in the beginning of my sophomore year in highschool, I was immediately intrigued by the skull and the front and the word Neanderthal on the cover. It is quite incredible that the author had made a backstory and an explanation how</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18239170479386313075">When I first saw this in the beginning of my sophomore year in highschool, I was immediately intrigued by the skull and the front and the word Neanderthal on the cover. I had know that a Neanderthal was an early human with super human strength and was about as smart as a human. <br /><br />I think that this book was made because of the theory that the legendary Bigfoot and Sasquatch are actually Neanderthals who've survived. It is quite incredible that the author had made a backstory and an explanation how the Neanderthal species had died out while Homo Sapiens had risen up to become dominant. <br /><br />It's also quite incredible that these creatures have telepathic powers, which humans have somehow lost. <br /><br />A lot of sex innuendo in it I'll admit. I wonder if its true that Steven Spielberg considered to making a movie of this. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('689xcs9IP4s43ZOs5IJwssRUO4YeY6G1Y6nLx21hsXOOG06hPZorcbQF5xea45YAjaP4n1e+5h8JoM5VofRHNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KC3knQR/dYRjhKlLhKueK2QbTYJqckImaiD+3jm5ha1N+dtO9q1hfu9c3fD6yniZLeyOmyOvBYwAKftM9Sxz6A==')})
  }

Rod Serling, an award-winning writer of television dramas, was the creator and host--and wrote more than 90 of the 156 episodes. \n\nThe series has since been shown around the world and the title is now a part of pop culture lore. Serling adapted 19 of his favorite teleplays into short stories, first published as a trio of paperback originals. The Twilight Zone: Complete Stories is a hardcover omnibus collection that includes all 19 stories and a historical introduction. \n\nThese stories have passed the test of time and are uniformly entertaining and well crafted. However, any reader who is a fan of the TV show may have difficulty allowing the stories to stand on their own without the filmed episodes intruding.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/55751.John_Darnton">About John Darnton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5694834940895082186">John Darnton has worked for The New York Times for forty years as a reporter, editor, and foreign correspondent. He is the recipient of two George Polk Awards and a Pulitzer Prize. He is also the author of five novels, including The Darwin Conspiracy and the best seller Neanderthal. He lives in New York. </span>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/55751.John_Darnton" class="actionLink moreLink">More about John Darnton...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
